WV","ticket_url":null,"ticket_type":null,"ticket_status":"unavailable","on_sale_datetime":null,"facebook_rsvp_url":"http://www.bandsintown.com/event/10942169?app_id=ONTOUR_1638&artist=Confederate+Railroad&came_from=67","description":"Schmitt's Saloon presents Confederate Railroad with special guest Marshall Lowry Band and Ward Davis \nConfederate Railroad first rolled onto the national country music scene in the early 90s with its unique style and sound.  Headed by founder and frontman Danny Shirley, the former backup band for both David Allan Coe and Johnny Paycheck got their big break by signing with Atlantic Records. The first single from their debut album (\"Confederate Railroad\") was \"She Took It Like A Man\". It went to No. 26, a preview of what was to come. \"The next two singles, \"Jesus and Mama\" and \"Queen of Memphis\" went to the top of the charts. Three more huge hits followed, \"Trashy Women\", \"When You Leave That Way You Can Never Go Back\", and \"She Never Cried\". \"Trashy\" would lead to a Grammy nomination and become their signature song. That album with six hits and nearly three million sales brought Confederate the Academy of Country Music's Best New Group Award in 1993 as well as numerous nominations from the Country Music Association and the British Country Music Foundation.  The second album, \"Notorious\", produced one of the group's most popular songs \"Daddy Never Was the Cadillac Kind\" which became a No. One video as well. \"Elvis and Andy\" and \"Summer in Dixie\" would further establish the Railroad as one of the most versatile acts in the business. This album would sell more than one million. Their overal totals are 18 charted hits and five million albums sold.  From rowdy country to raw emotion, a Confederate Railroad concert today covers a wide range of feelings. Young people will be there rocking to \"Trashy Women\", while their parents and even grandparents will likely be singing along to \"Jesus and Mama\". The band plays 100 or so dates each year. Whatever the venue, they are right at home…be it a fair, a club, or a biker show. Shirley, the lead singer and vocalist, and his mates, Mark Dufresne on drums, Wayne Secrest on bass, Rusty Hendrix on lead guitar and Bobby Randall on steel guitar, fiddle and vocals are obviously having fun right along with their appreciative audience. At the end of each show, the band stays around until every fan who wants an autograph, or to pose with the group for a picture or just say \"hello\" is taken care of. \nSpecial Guest \nCharles Marshall Lowry was born and raised in a small West Virginia town called Fairview, where he was introduced to country and gospel music at an early age. Surrounded by a family of musicians and pickers, Marshall picked up his first guitar at the age of 7, a weathered acoustic guitar that was a gift from his “Pa” Jack Crum. By age 11 his mother had him reading music and playing in his school’s band, while he and his Pa continued to pick and play on Saturday nights. \nThroughout a sometimes rocky childhood, Marshall’s guitar was always a constant. He honed his skills in bars, churches, school hallways, and anywhere else he could find a friendly ear. He was rarely without an instrument in his hand, and he quickly made a name for himself as a young musician to keep an eye on. \nMarshall bounced between several bands as he experimented with styles, acting as a frontman, bassist, lead guitarist, or whatever role was needed. He finally found a solid footing as lead guitarist and co-frontman of The New Relics, who toured with Marshall for five years and released 3 singles to country radio, the most popular of which, “Beautiful,” reached #54 on Billboard’s Hot Country chart. In The New Relics, Marshall refined his sound as a quick-picking country guitar slinger with a whisky-smooth voice. \nAfter his stint with The New Relics, Marshall formed The Marshall Lowry Band. Comprised of accomplished area musicians that Marshall played with for years, TMLB gained a fast and loyal regional following in North Central West Virginia. The band’s collective influences range from Johnny Cash to Brad Paisley to Gov’t Mule and the Allman Brothers Band. With his band, Marshall released his first EP, titled“Still Standing,” on January 1, 2012. \nThe Marshall Lowry Band recorded their first single, “Miles to Go,” in Nashville in the fall of 2013, and
